3:34:50
3 hours, 34 minutes, 50 seconds
Today we're going to be talking about productions for aentic systems.
3:34:54
3 hours, 34 minutes, 54 seconds
When most people hear the word valuation, they think about benchmarks.
3:34:58
3 hours, 34 minutes, 58 seconds
A model scores 90% on a benchmark. A new version scores 92%. The team celebrates.
3:35:04
3 hours, 35 minutes, 4 seconds
But agent systems have fundamentally changed what the evaluation means. Today the systems don't simply generate answers. They plan, they call tools,
3:35:13
3 hours, 35 minutes, 13 seconds
they retrieve information. They execute workflows. They interact with the production infrastructure. The question is no longer did the model generate the
3:35:20
3 hours, 35 minutes, 20 seconds
right answer. The question is did the system behave correctly. Today I would like to discuss how evaluation is
3:35:27
3 hours, 35 minutes, 27 seconds
evolving from model benchmarking into production infrastructure.
3:35:35
3 hours, 35 minutes, 35 seconds
This is the problem almost every AI organization is encountering today. Offline benchmarks continue improving.
3:35:41
3 hours, 35 minutes, 41 seconds
Yet production reliability often remains unpredictable. Why is that? Because benchmarks measure model capability.
3:35:48
3 hours, 35 minutes, 48 seconds
Production measures system behavior. A benchmark doesn't capture tool failure, API outage, context changes, user
3:35:55
3 hours, 35 minutes, 55 seconds
variability, longunning workflows. And as systems become more autonomous, the gap between the benchmark performance and production performance grows. The
3:36:03
3 hours, 36 minutes, 3 seconds
result is what many teams experience today. High benchmark scores as you can see, but unreliable production behavior.
3:36:14
3 hours, 36 minutes, 14 seconds
Traditional evaluation focus on outputs.
3:36:17
3 hours, 36 minutes, 17 seconds
But we should ask the question, did the model produce a correct answer? Agentic systems force us to ask a different question. Did the system behave
3:36:24
3 hours, 36 minutes, 24 seconds
correctly? Behavior includes planning quality, tool usage, execution, workflow execution, recovery from failures,
3:36:32
3 hours, 36 minutes, 32 seconds
decision making. In other words, we are moving from evaluating answers to evaluating workflows. And that requires fundamentally different evaluation architectures.
3:36:43
3 hours, 36 minutes, 43 seconds
Many teams still think hallucinations are the primary AI failure modes. In production, they are often just one category. Agentic systems introduce an
3:36:52
3 hours, 36 minutes, 52 seconds
entire hierarchy of failure modes. At the very foundation the memory failures, retrieable failures, safety failures. As you go up, you have to think about
3:37:01
3 hours, 37 minutes, 1 second
reasoning mistakes, poor planning, incorrect tool execution. At the highest layer, you have to think about multi- aent coordination failures. And this is
3:37:08
3 hours, 37 minutes, 8 seconds
why evaluating only model output misses the most production risks we observe.
3:37:15
3 hours, 37 minutes, 15 seconds
One of the most useful mindset shifts is to stop thinking like researchers and start thinking like a SR or a production
3:37:22
3 hours, 37 minutes, 22 seconds
engineer. S SR don't measure success using accuracy. They measure reliability, availability, latency, cost recovery and agentic systems require the
3:37:31
3 hours, 37 minutes, 31 seconds
same approach. The goal is not maximizing the benchmark scores. The goal is to maximize dependable outcomes.
3:37:37
3 hours, 37 minutes, 37 seconds
Reliability becomes the northstar metric. Accuracy becomes the only input.
3:37:47
3 hours, 37 minutes, 47 seconds
In this pyramid is how I think personally think about modern AI evaluation systems. At the bottom you can see there are benchmarks. They're useful. They're scalable. They're
3:37:55
3 hours, 37 minutes, 55 seconds
reputable. But the operational value is limited. In the middle there scenario based valuations. These simulate realistic workflows. And at the very top
3:38:04
3 hours, 38 minutes, 4 seconds
you see production telemetry. This is where the highest value valuation signals come from. The surprising insight is that the most evaluation data
3:38:11
3 hours, 38 minutes, 11 seconds
often comes from real users interacting with real systems.
